  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cc6b3d34-5088-4e53-b799-24754302141b'

<span id="freeTextContainer8343190604846390684">12 year old Theodore "Teddy" Roosevelt Fitzroy has got a murder on his hands and trouble on his tail. Henry, the hippopatamus at the brand-new nationally known FunJungle, has gone belly up.   <span id="freeText8343190604846390684" style="display:none">12 year old Theodore "Teddy" Roosevelt Fitzroy has got a murder on his hands and trouble on his tail. Henry, the hippopatamus at the brand-new nationally known FunJungle, has gone belly up. Even though it's claimed he died of natural causes, Teddy smells something fishy and it sure ain't the polar bear's lunch. Dealing with the zoo's top brass proves to be nothing but a waste of time. They want to see any trace of Henry's death disappear like yesterday's paper. So Teddy sets out to find the truth. With the help of Summer McCraken, a fiesty girl with secrets of her own, the two narrow down their prime suspects. Is it Martin Del Gato, FunJungle's head of operations who dislikes kids and hates animals even more? Or J.J McCraken, the owner of FunJungle and Summer's father, who has more concern for the dough he's raking in than the animals in the zoo? As their investigation goes on, Teddy gets squeezed on all sides to quit asking questions-- or Henry won't be the only one to turn up dead. The deeper Teddy and Summer get, the more the danger mounts -- because when it comes to hippo homicide, the truth can't be kept in a cage!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8343190604846390684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_112837414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112837414" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112837414?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">montambo montambo montambo</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=from-publisher-or-author">from-publisher-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=les-animaux">les-animaux</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=kiddiwinx">kiddiwinx</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112837414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer138487475186743267">first, look at the cover. now, look at the endpapers:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337522i/695093._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>how are you going to say "no" to that?? you're not. because not only is it a beautifully designed book, the story itself is great, and if i could stand to be around children, i would give them this book, because it is both fun and good for them, like flintstones vitamins. <br/><br/>i saw this on a cart in the basement at work while i was waiting for the elevator, and the colors attracted me. me being me, i yanked it out from the middle, causing a minor </span>
  <span id="freeText138487475186743267" style="display:none">first, look at the cover. now, look at the endpapers:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337522i/695093._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>how are you going to say "no" to that?? you're not. because not only is it a beautifully designed book, the story itself is great, and if i could stand to be around children, i would give them this book, because it is both fun and good for them, like flintstones vitamins. <br><br>i saw this on a cart in the basement at work while i was waiting for the elevator, and the colors attracted me. me being me, i yanked it out from the middle, causing a minor book avalanche. i sort of cleaned it up (sorry, kids department), but then the elevator came, and i ran on, clutching the book to my chest like some indiana jones prize, cackling guiltily to myself. i immediately emailed ariel to find out what she knew about it, and not only did she know the designer, but she sent me a copy of my own because she is truly the best.<br><br>like this book.<br><br>i really love this book. not only is it a great story about the world's best possible theme park-zoo, where the animals are respected and kept in enclosures which mimic their natural environments (with real snow! in texas!), but there is a great mystery at the center of it all - <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IUM7jl8S5AU&amp;feature=related" rel="nofollow noopener"> who murdered henry the hippo?</a> and why? <br><br>this is not a kiddie-kid book, it is not cutesy, but it is still fun; no mean feat. i think it would work really well read aloud, plus it has tons of animal facts that bring the animal kingdom alive for the little ones, and teach them about how to properly comport themselves at the zoo, and how to respect the animals and to recognize certain behaviors to know what is danger and what is not.<br><br>there is also a lot of poop in this book. and who doesn't like poop? i know plenty of adults who are fascinated by,and quite taken with, their own poop, but kids still like poop jokes, right? it is always appearing in a natural context, not scatology for scatology's sake, but there is a serious amount of poop in this book. moving on...<br><br>for you purists - there is absolutely no anthropomorphism here. it is a zoo story, with true animal facts and everything is done very respectfully and truly. i didn't know what to expect going into this - if there was going to be a kangaroo detective and a badger with a magnifying glass, but it was handled in the best way possible.<br><br>also, the last chapter is called "who did it", in case you get lazy. but you won't because it is a really great read. and not "a really great kids read". this spans age groups, provided you aren't the biggest of all possible book snobs. <br><br>just nice work all around.<br>a round of applause for simon and schuster...<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337522i/695094.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>and hippos!!<br><br><br>i was totally going to write a proust review tonight, but i got so excited by this that proust has to wait. i am not in the mood to write measured and intelligent right now - just summertime fun!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="138487475186743267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText48251343296614018" style="display:none">Fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8178.Carl_Hiaasen" title="Carl Hiaasen" rel="nofollow noopener">Carl Hiaasen</a>’s books <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13083.Hoot" title="Hoot by Carl Hiaasen" rel="nofollow noopener">Hoot</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13067.Flush" title="Flush by Carl Hiaasen" rel="nofollow noopener">Flush</a> will enjoy this middle grade mystery set at FunJungle, an exotic animal amusement park. When Henry the Hippo, the mascot of the newly-opened park, goes belly up, 12-year old Teddy thinks it would be fun to sneak into the autopsy. He’s been around animals his whole life, since his mom is a gorilla researcher and his dad a wildlife photographer, and he’s intrigued by Henry’s seemingly untimely demise. <br /><br />When he overhears that the hippo’s death might be a murder and that park officials plan to cover it up, he decides to solve it himself. But someone at the park wants to keep him quiet – can Teddy avoid the same fate at the hippo? This amusing read has a strong character in Teddy, a likeable 12-year old who will appeal to animal lovers. Not too scary but with plenty of suspense, this is a good choice for upper elementary and early middle school grades.</span>

The characters are fun and entertaining. There is a lot of running around kid-style, meaning kids will enjoy it.   <span id="freeText5525713766341426645" style="display:none">What a fun book. A murder mystery for kids! (Not young kids. I think 3-4th grade and up.) And it works, because the murder victim is a hippopotamus. The characters are fun and entertaining. There is a lot of running around kid-style, meaning kids will enjoy it. <span id="freeTextContainer16170895284007462508">This heart-warming and life-changing story about a boy and his free time will surely captivate and inspire the reader. This book should be required reading for all humans on planet earth. The power of the author's words can stir up deep emotional connections between ourselves and the book's main character. Hemingway, Shakespeare, and Dickens have nothing on whoever wrote this book. Put it next to the Bible on your bookshelf and your collection will be complete! Laugh, cry, stand in awe. No emoti</span>
  <span id="freeText16170895284007462508" style="display:none">This heart-warming and life-changing story about a boy and his free time will surely captivate and inspire the reader. This book should be required reading for all humans on planet earth. The power of the author's words can stir up deep emotional connections between ourselves and the book's main character. Hemingway, Shakespeare, and Dickens have nothing on whoever wrote this book. Put it next to the Bible on your bookshelf and your collection will be complete! Laugh, cry, stand in awe. No emotion goes untouched when reading this touching tale. Your measly, pathetic, tiresome existence will soon have meaning. Just read this damn book.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3217227227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2483445309942354599">A wonderful start to one of my favorite series, but there's something about this book that isn't as good as the other ones. The narration is also incredibly childish at times. Definitely didn't enjoy it as much as my first read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2682148244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2682148244" />
    <a title="Chris Blocker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/318724-chris-blocker"><img alt="Chris Blocker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460411481p2/318724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2682148244?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Blocker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Blocker" href="/user/show/318724-chris-blocker">Chris Blocker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/318724-chris-blocker?shelf=read-to-kids">read-to-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2682148244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16102139367201777863"><i>Belly Up</i> was not what I was expecting. I was expecting hilarity. Sure it has a dead hippo on the cover, but the cartoonish of it, plus the colors... Actually, <i>Belly Up</i> is rather morbid. It’s still great fun, but fun in the what’s-gonna-happen-next way, not in the oh-look-monkies! kind of way.<br/> <br/>Chapter 1 of <i>Belly Up</i> met my expectations. There’s a mischievous kid in a zoo, dodging the adults who want to put an end to his fun. And then there’s poop. Lots and lots of poo. Poo continues to make appear</span>
  <span id="freeText16102139367201777863" style="display:none"><i>Belly Up</i> was not what I was expecting. I was expecting hilarity. Sure it has a dead hippo on the cover, but the cartoonish of it, plus the colors... Actually, <i>Belly Up</i> is rather morbid. It’s still great fun, but fun in the what’s-gonna-happen-next way, not in the oh-look-monkies! kind of way.<br /> <br />Chapter 1 of <i>Belly Up</i> met my expectations. There’s a mischievous kid in a zoo, dodging the adults who want to put an end to his fun. And then there’s poop. Lots and lots of poo. Poo continues to make appearances throughout the novel, but it’s in this first chapter than poo really makes its grand entrance. I think I could argue that poop is actually the protagonist of this novel.<br /><br />That first chapter sets the stage for what ends up being a very different book. The story becomes increasingly darker as it goes on. There are still bits of humor from beginning to end, but they’re mixed in with a larger story that focuses on murder, attempted murder, and some all-out grossness. Seriously, the climax of this novel makes that fair scene from <i>
  <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XjrM8fkJMHE" rel="nofollow noopener">Problem Child 2</a>
</i> as sweet as cotton candy.<br /><br /><i>Belly Up</i> is a classic whodunit story told in a zoo. (And Agent Poop is on the case.) I’m not a big fan of the mystery genre for any age, so I’m not the intended audience, but I felt the formula was implemented well. The reveal was not surprising (I actually called it very early in the book) and the reason wasn’t entirely organic to the plot, but neither of these flaws kept the chase from being a fun ride. The characters were engaging. And there are animals, of course. This novel certainly succeeds as an entertaining mystery for children, especially those who laugh at poop.<br /><br />For those with objections to strong language, please note that this book uses language that may seem misplaced in a children’s book. These include multiple utterances of words such as bastard, ass, hell, and damn. Yeah, I’ve heard worse in a PG movie, but I still thought someone might want to know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16102139367201777863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shruti S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13862757-shruti-s"><img alt="Shruti S" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466496559?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shruti S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shruti S" href="/user/show/13862757-shruti-s">Shruti S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416987321" href="/book/show/10475716-belly-up">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466496559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8761495939034164401">Dec 4, 2012<br/><br/>I recently finished reading the Lone Star book "Belly Up" by Stuart Gibbs. Growing up in America's most popular theme park would sound fun, right? Wrong! Teddy Fitzroy lives there and runs into trouble everyday because he is lonely and bored. The worst part for Teddy, is Henry the hippopotamus, the park's mascot. Lazy, nasty,and obnoxious are some of the never-ending list of negative words to describe Henry. But no one could hate him enough to land him belly up, which he does anyways.</span>
  <span id="freeText8761495939034164401" style="display:none">Dec 4, 2012<br /><br />I recently finished reading the Lone Star book "Belly Up" by Stuart Gibbs. Growing up in America's most popular theme park would sound fun, right? Wrong! Teddy Fitzroy lives there and runs into trouble everyday because he is lonely and bored. The worst part for Teddy, is Henry the hippopotamus, the park's mascot. Lazy, nasty,and obnoxious are some of the never-ending list of negative words to describe Henry. But no one could hate him enough to land him belly up, which he does anyways. Tedd jumps on to the case along with Summer McCracken, the founder/owner's famous daughter. Can they solve the homicide before they too land belly up? Packed with humor, mystery, and crime, this investigation was unique and showed the development of Tedd and Summer's friendship. This book was so detailed, it made me want to go there even though I knew it was'nt a real place. I however, could not relate to any of the character's feelings because I have not been in any situation like that. Though I could admire certain qualities like their courage and out of the box thinking. I was laughing when Henry was shooting poo at the visitors and was at the edge of my seat when Teddy was trapped with a black mamba(the most vicious snake) in a dark room. The book had spurts of action throughout the story, until the climax.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to people who like animal based stories and children-solving mystery books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8761495939034164401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058227-chelsey?shelf=best-beloved">best-beloved</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058227-chelsey?shelf=read-aloud-to-future-children">read-aloud-to-future-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058227-chelsey?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058227-chelsey?shelf=as-good-as-they-say-it-is">as-good-as-they-say-it-is</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454243980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5122683151694308222">I was beginning to wonder if it was even possible to write a fantastic mystery for middle grade readers. I was wrong!<br/><br/>The only downsides here are a mention of marijuana, and the phrase "hauling ass," which is going to be off-putting to some parents. But don't let that stop you from giving it to kids with reckless abandon!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_369006286" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369006286" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3188331-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264809988p2/3188331.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369006286?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/3188331-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3188331-nancy?shelf=mark-twain-2012-nominees">mark-twain-2012-nominees</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3188331-nancy?shelf=books-read-in-2012">books-read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3188331-nancy?shelf=children-s-book-2012">children-s-book-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369006286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12539592014619226879">Teddy, a 12-year-old, grew up in the Congo of Africa because his mother is a famous gorilla researcher on the order of Diane Fossey and his father is a famous wildlife photographer. They now live in a trailer in Texas on the outskirts of FunJungle, the largest zoo/Disneyworld type attraction in the USA, where his parents are employed. The mascot of the park, Henry the Hippo, a mean and messy animal who is not liked by many who have been injured by him, ends up suspiciously dead. Teddy and Summer</span>
  <span id="freeText12539592014619226879" style="display:none">Teddy, a 12-year-old, grew up in the Congo of Africa because his mother is a famous gorilla researcher on the order of Diane Fossey and his father is a famous wildlife photographer. They now live in a trailer in Texas on the outskirts of FunJungle, the largest zoo/Disneyworld type attraction in the USA, where his parents are employed. The mascot of the park, Henry the Hippo, a mean and messy animal who is not liked by many who have been injured by him, ends up suspiciously dead. Teddy and Summer, a Paris Hilton-type only 13-years-old, the daughter of the rich tycoon who owns the theme park are the only one who take on the investigation while adults and police seem to ignore the evidence. Soon Teddy seems to be the next target for danger and possible death. <br /> I liked the story because it had informative facts about animals, conservation and the role of zoos in a developing global world where animal habitat is disappearing. The story was a page turner. Teddy's voice was strong and I thought sometimes inappropriate for the 3rd and 4th graders who will be reading this. This is the same content that I think will appeal to that age student, especially boys. They may find it hilarious.<br /> I liked that this kid eventually shared his fears and problems with the caring adults in his life. So often fiction authors of this age group seem to think the kid characters must take on everything alone. This handling of the kid/adult relationship was more realistic and made a good point that sometimes you need to get adult help. It didn't detract from the kid characters' bravery and intelligence, just enhanced it.<br /> It reads like a screen play for a movie, very exciting and visual with chase scenes and almost jungle-like dangers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12539592014619226879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1078646672" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1078646672" />
    <a title="Addie T" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34552018-addie-t"><img alt="Addie T" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409693040p2/34552018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1078646672?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addie T" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addie T" href="/user/show/34552018-addie-t">Addie T</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416987321" href="/book/show/10475716-belly-up">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1078646672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5967248899483111024">12 year old, Teddy Fitzroy has spent all of his life around animals. He grew up in the Congo and now both his parents work at FunJungle, the largest zoo attraction in the U.S. It is located in Texas, 30 minutes away from any real towns. The park is owned by J.J. McCracken, famous for making a lot of money. Teddy's life pretty much stays the same at the zoo until one day they find Henry the Hippo, the parks mascot, laying belly up in his pen. Teddy finds this very unusual considering the park has</span>
  <span id="freeText5967248899483111024" style="display:none">12 year old, Teddy Fitzroy has spent all of his life around animals. He grew up in the Congo and now both his parents work at FunJungle, the largest zoo attraction in the U.S. It is located in Texas, 30 minutes away from any real towns. The park is owned by J.J. McCracken, famous for making a lot of money. Teddy's life pretty much stays the same at the zoo until one day they find Henry the Hippo, the parks mascot, laying belly up in his pen. Teddy finds this very unusual considering the park has opened 2 weeks ago. He sneaks into the autopsy and overhears that Henry might have been murdered! Teddy is immediately investigating. Though he tells few people, none believe him. When superstar Summer McCracken, J.J.'s McCraken's daughter, shows up he decides to tell her while she is being mobbed by the paparazzi. She has no idea who Teddy is, but decides to help him investigate. <br /><br />	The theme of the story is to trust yourself. Teddy believes that Henry was murdered, but no one listens to him. He will not stop until he can prove that Henry was murdered. This is an action packed mystery that never has a dull moment. I liked this book because I could never tell what was going to happen and it was informative about animals. This story is told in first person of Teddy's perspective. I could relate to Teddy because I am always investigating rumors I hear. Teddy told Buck every thing he knew about Henry being murdered and Buck told him to stop investigating. That does not stop Teddy! I would definitely recommend this book for both boys and girls ages 11-13.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5967248899483111024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1001804470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001804470" />
    <a title="Ryan Slattery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32663511-ryan-slattery"><img alt="Ryan Slattery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444784602p2/32663511.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001804470?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Slattery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Slattery" href="/user/show/32663511-ryan-slattery">Ryan Slattery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001804470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17924071806150576238">This is Stuart Gibbs' first novel, but I read his book Spy School (I gave 5 stars) before reading this.<br/><br/>I rated this with 4 stars because had I not read Spy School and loved it, I might have put this book down after the first couple chapters.<br/><br/>But I didn't, and I am very glad I didn't. It's basically a Whodunit (like Spy School), only this time I never was able to guess the right suspect and questioned everyone's involvement at various times.<br/><br/>The chase scene at the end was masterfully done and I cou</span>
  <span id="freeText17924071806150576238" style="display:none">This is Stuart Gibbs' first novel, but I read his book Spy School (I gave 5 stars) before reading this.<br /><br />I rated this with 4 stars because had I not read Spy School and loved it, I might have put this book down after the first couple chapters.<br /><br />But I didn't, and I am very glad I didn't. It's basically a Whodunit (like Spy School), only this time I never was able to guess the right suspect and questioned everyone's involvement at various times.<br /><br />The chase scene at the end was masterfully done and I couldn't get enough by the end of the book.<br /><br />So why not 5 stars?<br /><br />Teddy (the main character) gets a little too expositional a little too often and describes things overmuch (my opinion). The second reason was that the author violates Teddy's POV a few times, which took me out of the story. For instance he describes not just that his father is surprised by something, but has telepathic powers and tells me exactly what surprised him. Or Teddy will tell me that Summer was embarrassed, when her embarrassment isn't a feeling he's privy to, unless he sees her acting embarrassed (but those details weren't there).<br /><br />Overall, I think I'll buy Spy Camp before I buy Poached, but I'll probably buy both at some point anyway because Stuart Gibbs can write a fun book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17924071806150576238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7931478906574175185" style="display:none">I decided to read Belly Up because it is on the NC children's book award list for 2013. Also I love the covers. My husband even said he would be sad when I finished the book because he enjoyed looking at the cover from across the room. smile.... I thought the book was going to be cute like he cover. Oh my was I wrong. This is a mystery that will keep you wondering up until the end. Of course the murder victim is a crotchety hippo that is the mascot for FunJungle, the most visited tourist attraction in the nation. Teddy, is a 12 year old boy who living at the zoo with his parents who work there with animals. Teddy decides to conduct his own investigations into Henry's death, which put his life in danger. Lots of intrigue, little bit of romance, humor and certainly grossness. If you love animals, you should enjoy this mystery. I think this is Stuart Gibbs first novel. He could not have chosen a better ending to this mystery. </span>

  <span id="freeText8654808886466910209" style="display:none">I read this book many years ago, but I still remember the endless love I have for it. This book was probably the first time I dealt with the true sadness of finishing such an amazing book. One you don't want to let go of. </span>

<div id="review_108310425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108310425" />
    <a title="Christiane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1250314-christiane"><img alt="Christiane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226093599p2/1250314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108310425?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christiane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christiane" href="/user/show/1250314-christiane">Christiane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250314-christiane?shelf=summer-reading">summer-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250314-christiane?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108310425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer489825017502006321">Twelve-year-old Teddy investigates when a popular Texas zoo’s star attraction—Henry the hippopotamus—is murdered. One of my most requested titles this summer. The cover art is great, and the premise is hard to beat. Teddy lives in a combination zoo/amusement park and is the only one who realizes that Henry’s murder is being covered up by park officials. Fun mystery with wild animals and a disgusting gross-out scene near the end (you’ll definitely know it when you read it!).</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z/ieVezPqFFrEhqTbbPDRfjE4fI/EmgBBHf6h+dTe69wyOssrkUbh9/f2kA0pOGqaT7P40QjVh+3rCPs1s+WAQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
